Refuting the Claim of Negligence in Imam Appointment
Nasafi refutes the claim that not appointing an imam would be negligence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi refutes the argument that the Prophet's not explicitly appointing an imam would be negligence, and the alternative basis for imam selection.

Core Idea
The Prophet guided the community without explicit text, through general indications.

Some argue that if the Prophet had not explicitly named a successor, he would have neglected a vital duty and caused chaos. Nasafi counters this, affirming the Prophet's wisdom and care. In this passage, he explains that the Prophet did not leave the matter unguided but provided signs (dalalah) indicating worthiness—a middle path between explicit appointment and total silence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage slowly, then its translation. Notice the rhythm: a claim is stated, then rejected, then an alternative is offered.
Pay attention to the term 'نص' (explicit text) versus 'دلالة' (indication).
2
Identify the opposing argument
The passage begins by quoting the claim: 'If he did not appoint an imam, he would have neglected the community.' Understand why this argument might seem persuasive.
This claim rests on the assumption that only explicit appointment can safeguard the community.
3
Recognize the refutation
Nasafi calls the claim false and explains why: the Prophet did establish guidance ('دلالة') about who is most entitled to leadership, just not through explicit text ('نص').
This refutation preserves the Prophet's perfection while rejecting a specific method.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this argument supports the legitimacy of consultation (shura) and community choice, as exemplified at Saqifa.
This passage is a key Maturidi response to the Shi'a position on nass.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لو لم ينص على إمام لضيَّع الأمة. قول باطل] وما يزعمون أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لو لم ينص على إمامة أحد لضيع أعظم أمور الأمة وأوقعهم في أفحش فتنة، وهذا لا يليق به عليه السلام. كلام باطل، فإن النبي عليه السلام قد أقام الدلالة على الأحق بذلك لكن لا بطريق النص على ما نبين.
"If he did not appoint an imam, he would have neglected the community." A false statement. And what they claim that the Prophet, peace be upon him, if he did not appoint someone as imam, he would have neglected the greatest of the community's affairs and thrown them into the most heinous tribulation, and this is not befitting of him, peace be upon him. It is a false statement. For the Prophet, peace be upon him, did establish the indication (dalalah) of who is most entitled to that, but not by the way of explicit text (nass), as we will explain.
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage refutes the argument that the Prophet must have explicitly appointed an imam, otherwise he would have neglected a great duty and caused fitna. The author states that this is false; the Prophet did not neglect the matter, but he provided general indications (dalalah) of who is most worthy of leadership, not an explicit text. The implication is that the method of appointment was through consultation and the community's choice, as demonstrated at Saqifa. The author promises to explain further.

Key Terms
نص
إمامة
ضياع
دلالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Prophet must have explicitly named a successor, otherwise his mission would be incomplete and the community would be left in confusion and sin.
Correction: The Prophet provided sufficient guidance through indications (dalalah) of worthiness, not necessarily explicit text. The community's responsibility to select a leader based on those indications is part of his perfect guidance.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, how did the Prophet indicate the rightful imam?
A) Through explicit texts naming the imam
B) Through general indications of worthiness
C) By leaving it to the community without any guidance
D) Through a divine revelation after his death

Key Takeaway
Nasafi refutes the necessity of an explicit appointment (nass) for the imam, affirming that the Prophet's guidance through indications (dalalah) is sufficient and preserves his perfection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that the guidance Allah has given through general principles (like the Prophet's indications) is enough for you to fulfil your responsibilities, or do you secretly wish for explicit commands for every decision? What would change if you trusted that sufficiency today?
?
When you face a difficult community matter (family, masjid, work), do you actively seek the 'indications' (dalalah) of the correct path, or do you wait for someone to give you an explicit order, excusing yourself from action? How has this affected your leadership or participation?
?
The opponents argued that lack of explicit text implies neglect. Have you ever used the excuse that 'I wasn't told explicitly' to avoid doing something you knew was right? Will you commit to acting on the clear indications Allah has given you, even without a direct command?

The Case Against an Explicit Text for 'Ali's Imamate
The author presents two historical arguments against the Shi'a claim of explicit nass.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses historical reasoning to refute the claim that there was an explicit textual designation (nass) for 'Ali's imamate.

Core Idea
If a clear text existed, why didn't the Ansar accept it and why didn't 'Ali use it?

Imam al-Nasafi opens his refutation by pointing to two striking historical facts. First, the Ansar of Medina—who were present at Saqifa—did not act as if any explicit divine appointment existed for 'Ali. Second, during his own caliphate, 'Ali himself never cited such a text. This lesson examines these arguments and their logical force.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the Ansar's acceptance
Read the passage that contrasts the Ansar's rejection of an alleged nass with their acceptance of the general Quraysh principle.
Notice the author's use of the Saqifa event.
2
Consider the question about 'Ali's silence
The author asks why 'Ali did not narrate the nass during his caliphate when he had support. Think about the implications.
The author preempts the excuse of cowardice by invoking 'Ali's bravery.
3
Identify the conclusion
The author concludes that 'Ali's surrender of the caliphate indicates he had no knowledge of any text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من الأوس والخزرج ولم يعاونوه ولم يقبلوا النص عليه ولم ينقادوا لذلك، وقد انقادوا لقول النبي عليه السلام: الأئمة من قريش حين روى لهم يوم سقيفة بني ساعدة، وكيف لم يرو على الله ذلك النص زمان خلافته وكثرة أتباعه وشيعته ومحبيه على من نابذه وناصبه الحرب؟ وكيف يتوهم منه تسليم ما هو أحق به من غيره إلى من ليس بأهل له جبنًا منه وفشلاً، والشجاعة شجعته والاعتماد على قول الرسول عليه السلام اعتماده والثقة بذلك ثقته، وقد وعده النبي عليه السلام أنه يقتل الناكثين وفيه إيقاع الأمن له عن القتل ونزول البلاء به دون مضي ذلك على يده فإذا كان سلم الأمر، دل أنه إنما أسلم لأنه لم يعرف لنفسه من الرسول عليه السلام إليه عهد أو لا ثبت له منه نص فيه أو وصية.

ثم هل يتوهم في العادات الجارية كتمان حديث اشتهر وثبت في قوم لا يتصور تواطؤهم على ذلك، ولو جاز هذا لجاز اشتهار الكذب وروايته عن قوم هذا وصفهم، وهذا كله جهالة لا يدانيها جهالة. ولولا تفاقم الأمر في زماننا هذا من الطاعنين على الصديق ونفاة إمامته الجاعلين ذلك ذريعة إلى ما يرومون من إبطال الدين وإثبات الإلحاد لما بالغت كل هذه المبالغة في ذلك، لظهوره عوار على من له أدنى لب والله الموفق.
From the Aws and Khazraj, they did not help him and did not accept the explicit text (nass) concerning him and did not submit to that, yet they submitted to the statement of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'The leaders are from Quraysh' when he narrated to them on the day of Saqifat Bani Sa'idah. How did 'Ali not narrate that text during his caliphate and the abundance of his followers, partisans, and lovers over those who opposed him and waged war against him? And how can it be imagined from him that he would surrender what he is more entitled to than others to someone who is not worthy of it out of cowardice and failure, while his courage is courageous and his reliance on the word of the Messenger, peace be upon him, is his reliance and his trust in that is his trust? And the Prophet, peace be upon him, had promised him that he would kill the breakers of the covenant (al-nakithin) and in that there is security for him from killing and the descent of calamity upon him without that happening by his hand. So when he surrendered the matter, it indicates that he only surrendered because he did not know for himself from the Messenger, peace be upon him, a covenant (ʿahd) or a text (nass) or a will (wasiyya) established for him.

Then is it imagined in current customs to conceal a hadith that became widespread and established among a people whose collusion upon that is inconceivable? And if this were permissible, then the widespread narration of lying would be permissible from people of this description. And all of this is ignorance that no ignorance can approach. And were it not for the gravity of the matter in our time from those who attack al-Siddiq and deny his imamate, making that a means to what they aim at of invalidating the religion and establishing atheism, I would not have gone to all this extent in that, because its flaw is apparent to anyone with the least intellect. And Allah is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Shi'a claim that there was an explicit textual designation (nass) for 'Ali's imamate. The author, Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi, presents several arguments. First, he notes that the Ansar (Aws and Khazraj) did not accept such a nass, yet they readily accepted the Prophet's general statement 'The leaders are from Quraysh' at Saqifa. If a clear nass for 'Ali existed, why would 'Ali himself not narrate it during his caliphate when he had overwhelming support? Second, the author argues that it is unimaginable that a tradition so widely known could be concealed by a group too large to conspire—if such concealment were possible, then lying could become widespread. The author concludes that the claim is pure ignorance. He then states that he only delves into this detail because of the attacks on Abu Bakr (al-Siddiq) in his time, who deny his imamate as a pretext for undermining Islam.

Key Terms
نص (nass)
إمامة (imama)
قريش (Quraysh)
سقيفة (Saqifa)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that the Prophet explicitly designated 'Ali as his successor by name, but that this text was suppressed or ignored.
Correction: The author argues that the historical behavior of both the Ansar and 'Ali himself disproves the existence of any such explicit text. If it existed, the Ansar would have heard it, and 'Ali would have used it.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why does the fact that the Ansar accepted the statement 'al-aimmatu min Quraysh' but rejected the nass indicate that there was no explicit text for 'Ali?
A) The Ansar disliked 'Ali.
B) The Ansar's behavior shows they were not aware of any explicit text.
C) The Prophet's statement was more authoritative.
D) The Ansar were not reliable narrators.

Key Takeaway
The author uses the historical behavior of the Ansar and 'Ali to argue that no explicit text designating 'Ali as caliph existed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Ali's courage is unquestioned, yet he did not assert a claim to leadership based on a text. Is there any right you believe you have but are not acting on because of fear or doubt? What does this passage challenge you to re-examine about your own assumptions regarding divine support?
?
The Ansar accepted the general principle that leaders are from Quraysh over a specific claim for Ali. When faced with a general principle that conflicts with a specific personal desire, which do you tend to follow? How does this apply to your obedience to Allah's commands even when they contradict your preferences?
?
The passage argues that Ali's surrender indicates he had no knowledge of a text. Consider a time when you remained silent about an important truth. Was it due to lack of certainty or due to weakness? What would it take for you to speak with the same confidence that Ali would have if he had a text?

The Impossibility of Concealing an Established Narration
The author presents a methodological argument against the possibility of concealing a widely known hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's argument that a widely known hadith cannot be hidden by a large group, and why this refutes the Shi'a claim.

Core Idea
A widely attested tradition cannot be concealed by tawatur.

After establishing that the historical record does not support a nass, the author turns to a broader methodological argument. He asserts that if a hadith was truly widespread and firmly established among the Companions, it would be impossible for them to collude in hiding it. This principle from hadith criticism undercuts any claim of a suppressed text.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage starting with 'ثم هل يتوهم'
Read the second part of the source, which contains the methodological argument. Notice the rhetorical question.
2
Understand the principle of tawatur
The author argues that a mutawatir hadith cannot be hidden. If it were possible, then falsehood could also become widespread.
This is a key principle in hadith criticism.
3
Note the author's concluding remarks
Read the final sentences where the author explains his motivation and emphasizes the obviousness of the flaw in the opposing view.
The author links the denial of Abu Bakr's imamate to a broader attack on Islam.

The Imamate by Election: One Qualified Person Suffices
Nasafi argues for election by a single qualified person.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's argument that the imamate is established through election (ikhtiyar) and that a single qualified mujtahid can validly contract it, based on historical precedents.

Core Idea
One qualified mujtahid can contract the imamate—no consensus required.

After establishing that the caliphate is not by explicit designation (nass), Imam Nasafi turns to the method of election. He argues that a single qualified person (mujtahid) can contract the imamate for a suitable candidate, and this contract is binding. This lesson walks through his reasoning and the historical evidence from the early Muslim community.

Guided Path
1
Set the context: nass is refuted
Recall that previous arguments refuted the idea that the imamate is established by explicit designation (nass). Now, the only valid method is election (ikhtiyar).
This sets the stage for the discussion.
2
Understand the Ash'ari position
Nasafi reports from al-Ash'ari that a single mujtahid can contract the imamate for a suitable person at the death of an imam. This contract is binding on others.
Nasafi does not find a clear Maturidi doctrine on this.
3
Examine the rejection of consensus
Nasafi argues that requiring consensus (ijma') delays the imamate beyond the time of need, and the Companions did not require it. Numbers do not matter.
Once consensus is not a condition, one person's contract is as valid as many.
4
Study the historical proofs
Two examples: (1) At Saqifah, 'Umar proposed Abu 'Ubaydah, who deferred to Abu Bakr, and 'Umar pledged allegiance—showing a single contract. (2) Abu Bakr appointed 'Umar alone, and the ummah accepted.
These prove the validity of a single contract.
5
Note the additional condition of witnesses
Some Maturidi scholars added that the contract must be in the presence of witnesses to prevent secret claims, similar to marriage.
This ensures transparency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إذا بطل ثبوت الخلافة بالنص ثبت أنها تثبت بالاختيار ثم للناس كلام في كيفية ذلك ولم أقف فيه على مذهب مشايخنا - رحمهم الله تعالى. وروى عن الأشعري أن واحدا من أهل الاجتهاد لو اجتهد في زمان موت إمام ورأى أسباب الصلاحية في أحد ثابتة فعقد له الإمامة انعقدت له، وليس لغيره بعد ذلك أن يخالفه ولا وجه إلى اشتراط الإجماع اليوم لما فيه من تأخير الإمامة عن وقت الحاجة إليها لو شرط فيها الإجماع، على أن الصحابة لم يشترطوا فيها الإجماع عند الاختيار والمبايعة، وإنما اعتبروا وجود العقد ثم أوجبوا المبايعة بعد ذلك. ثم الإجماع إذا خرج من أن يكون شرطا لم يكن عدد أولي من عدد فسقط اعتباره لثبوت التعارض وانعدام الترجيح. ويستدل على صحة هذا القول بما روي عن عمر أنه قال يوم السقيفة لأبي عبيدة: ابسط يدك أبايعك فقال له أبو عبيدة: أقول هذا وأبو بكر حاضر - فعلم من رأيه أنه يراه أولى، وأبو عبيدة أمين الأمة لا يخون، والأمة تعتمد على قوله فبايع أبا بكر وانعقدت إمامته وانبرمت، فدل هذا على أنها تنعقد بعقد واحد، وكذا استدلوا عليه بعقد أبي بكر لعمر واستخلافه له من غير استعانة بغيره، وجوزت الأمة ذلك وبايعوا عمر فكان هذا دليلاً أن الإمامة تنعقد بعقد واحد بإجماع المسلمين، والله الموفق. إلا أنه أضاف قال بعض أصحابنا: لابد من جريان العقد بمشهد من الشهود فإنه لو لم يشترط ذلك لم نأمن أن يدع مدع عقدًا سرًا متقدما على الحق المظهر المبطن، وليست الإمامة أحط رتبة من النكاح وقد شرط فيه الإعلان.
Then, if the establishment of the caliphate by explicit designation (nass) is invalid, it is established that it is established by choice (al-ikhtiyar). Then people have discussion about the modality of that, and I have not come across the doctrine of our scholars (may Allah have mercy on them) concerning it. It is narrated from al-Ash'ari that if one of the people of ijtihad, at the time of the death of an imam, exercised ijtihad and saw the reasons of suitability in someone as established, and contracted the imamate for him, it would be contracted for him, and it is not for anyone else afterwards to oppose him. And there is no justification for stipulating consensus (ijma') today, because of the delay of the imamate from the time of need if consensus were stipulated, especially since the Companions did not stipulate consensus in their choice and oath of allegiance. They only considered the existence of the contract, then they required the oath of allegiance afterwards. Then, if consensus ceases to be a condition, one number is not more entitled than another number, so its consideration falls due to the establishment of conflict and lack of preponderance. The soundness of this view is argued by what is narrated from 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said on the day of Saqifah to Abu 'Ubaydah: "Extend your hand so that I may pledge allegiance to you." Abu 'Ubaydah said to him: "Shall I say this when Abu Bakr is present?" So it was known from his opinion that he considered him more worthy. And Abu 'Ubaydah is the trustee of the ummah, he does not betray, and the ummah relies on his statement. So he pledged allegiance to Abu Bakr, and his imamate was contracted and concluded. This indicates that it is contracted by a single contract. Similarly, they argued by the contract of Abu Bakr for 'Umar and his appointing him as successor without seeking help from anyone else, and the ummah permitted that and pledged allegiance to 'Umar. This was evidence that the imamate is contracted by a single contract by the consensus of the Muslims. And Allah is the Grantor of success. However, some of our companions added: It is necessary for the contract to take place in the presence of witnesses, because if that were not stipulated, we would not be secure from a claimant claiming a secret contract prior to the true, manifest, hidden right. And the imamate is not inferior in rank to marriage, and publicity has been stipulated in it.
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage is a systematic argument for the method of selecting an imam (caliph). After establishing that the caliphate is not by explicit designation (nass) from the Prophet, the author proves that it is established by choice (ikhtiyar)—i.e., election. He then addresses the modality: he mentions that he did not find a definitive doctrine from his own Maturidi scholars, but he reports from Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari that a single qualified person (mujtahid) can contract the imamate for a suitable person when the previous imam dies. This contract is binding, and no one else can oppose it. He rejects the necessity of consensus (ijma') in the election because requiring it would delay the imamate beyond the time of need, and because the Companions themselves did not require it—they only considered the existence of a valid contract, after which they gave the oath of allegiance (bay'a). Once consensus is not required, numbers do not matter; one person's contract is as valid as that of many. He provides two historical proofs: (1) At Saqifah, 'Umar proposed Abu 'Ubaydah as caliph, but Abu 'Ubaydah deferred to Abu Bakr, and then 'Umar and others pledged allegiance to Abu Bakr, showing that a single contract (by 'Umar's proposal and Abu 'Ubaydah's refusal) led to the imamate. (2) Abu Bakr appointed 'Umar as his successor by a single contract without consulting others, and the ummah accepted it. Both cases demonstrate that the imamate is validly contracted by a single qualified person. The author then adds a clarification from some of his companions: the contract must be made in the presence of witnesses to prevent secret claims that undermine the public right; this is analogous to marriage, which requires publicity.

Key Terms
خلافة (khilafa)
نص (nass)
اختيار (ikhtiyar)
إجماع (ijma')
عقد (aqd)
بيعة (bay'a)
اجتهاد (ijtihad)
أشعري (Ash'ari)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That a caliph must be elected by a large council or by universal consensus.
Correction: This passage proves that one qualified person suffices to contract the imamate, as shown by the actions of the Companions.

Checkpoint
What is the main evidence given for the imamate being contracted by a single contract?
A) The Quranic verse on consultation
B) The incident of Saqifah where 'Umar pledged allegiance to Abu Bakr after Abu 'Ubaydah deferred
C) The appointment of 'Ali by the Prophet at Ghadir Khumm
D) The consensus of all Muslims at the time of Abu Bakr

Key Takeaway
Nasafi proves that the imamate is validly contracted by a single qualified mujtahid, as shown by the actions of the Companions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a decision, do you often hide behind a desire for consensus to avoid personal responsibility? This lesson shows that one qualified person's judgment can suffice. Where in your life right now do you need to step up and make a decision alone, trusting your qualifications (or those of a trusted person) rather than waiting for everyone's approval? What specific action will you take today?
?
The Companions accepted Abu Bakr's appointment by a single contract. How does their trust in a qualified person contrast with your own hesitation to trust qualified leaders? Is there a qualified person in your community whose judgment you have been resisting because you wanted a say? Will you commit to supporting that person's decision this week, even if you were not part of the process?
?
The passage warns against secret contracts that undermine the truth. Is there any area of your life—family, work, faith—where you are keeping decisions hidden to avoid accountability? What would it cost you to bring that matter into the light, and what step can you take this week to ensure transparency and truthfulness?

Rejecting Consensus as a Condition for Imama
Al-Nasafi argues that consensus is not a condition for imama.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Al-Nasafi argues that consensus (ijma') is not a condition for the appointment of an imam, and that a single qualified person's contract suffices.

Core Idea
A single qualified person's contract is enough; consensus would cause harmful delay.

Al-Nasafi begins by establishing that since explicit designation (nass) is invalid, the caliphate is established by choice. He then reports a view from al-Ash'ari that a single mujtahid can contract the imama. Crucially, he argues that requiring consensus would delay the appointment, and that the Companions did not require it. This lesson presents the core argument against consensus as a necessary condition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on rejection of consensus
Read the Arabic and translation carefully, noting the reasons given against requiring ijma'.
Pay attention to the phrase 'ولا وجه إلى اشتراط الإجماع'.
2
Identify the three reasons
Al-Nasafi gives three reasons: delay, Companion practice, and the argument about numbers. List them.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this argument matters for the legitimacy of early caliphates and for later political theory.
The absence of consensus requirement allows for quick succession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إذا بطل ثبوت الخلافة بالنص ثبت أنها تثبت بالاختيار ثم للناس كلام في كيفية ذلك (۱) ولم أقف فيه على مذهب مشايخنا - رحمهم الله تعالى. وروى عن الأشعري أن واحدا من أهل الاجتهاد لو (۲) اجتهد في زمان موت إمام ورأى أسباب الصلاحية في أحد ثابتة فعقد له الإمامة انعقدت له، وليس لغيره بعد ذلك أن يخالفه (۳) ولا وجه إلى اشتراط الإجماع اليوم لما فيه من تأخير الإمامة عن وقت الحاجة إليها لو شرط فيها الإجماع، على أن الصحابة لم يشترطوا فيها الإجماع عند الاختيار والمبايعة، وإنما اعتبروا وجود العقد ثم أوجبوا المبايعة بعد ذلك. ثم الإجماع (٤) إذا خرج من أن يكون شرطا لم يكن عدد أولي من عدد فسقط اعتباره لثبوت التعارض وانعدام الترجيح. ويستدل على صحة هذا القول بما روي عن عمر ه أنه قال يوم السقيفة لأبي عبيدة ه: - ابسط يدك أبايعك فقال له أبو عبيدة: أقول هذا وأبو بكر حاضر - فعلم من رأيه أنه يراه أولى، وأبو عبيدة أمين الأمة لا يخون، والأمة تعتمد على قوله فبايع أبا بكر الله الله وانعقدت إمامته وانبرمت، فدل هذا على أنها تنعقد بعقد واحد، وكذا استدلوا عليه بعقد أبي بكر لعمر واستخلافه له من غير () استعانة بغيره، وجوزت الأمة ذلك وبايعوا عمر الله فكان هذا دليلاً أن الإمامة تنعقد بعقد واحد بإجماع المسلمين(٦)، والله الموفق.
Then if the establishment of the caliphate by explicit designation (nass) is invalid, it is established that it is established by choice (ikhtiyar). Then people have discussion concerning the modality of that (1), and I have not come across a doctrine of our scholars (may Allah have mercy on them) regarding it. It is narrated from al-Ash'ari that if one of the people of ijtihad (2) exerts effort at the time of the death of an imam and sees the causes of suitability in someone, and contracts the imama for him, it is contracted for him, and no one else after that may oppose him (3). There is no basis for requiring consensus (ijma') today because of the delay of the imama from the time of need that would occur if consensus were required. Moreover, the Companions did not require consensus at the time of choice and pledge of allegiance; rather they considered the existence of the contract and then required the pledge of allegiance after that. Then consensus (4), if it ceases to be a condition, a greater number is not [better] than a lesser number, so its consideration falls due to the establishment of conflict and lack of preponderance. The correctness of this statement is supported by what is narrated from 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said on the day of Saqifa to Abu 'Ubayda (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Extend your hand, I give you the pledge of allegiance.' Abu 'Ubayda said to him: 'I say this while Abu Bakr is present?' So it was known from his opinion that he considered him more worthy. Abu 'Ubayda is the trustee of the community, he does not betray, and the community relies on his word. So he gave the pledge of allegiance to Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him), and his imama was contracted and completed. This indicates that it is contracted by a single contract. Similarly, they argued from Abu Bakr's contract for 'Umar and his appointment of him as successor without seeking help from others, and the community permitted that and gave the pledge of allegiance to 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him). This was evidence that the imama is contracted by a single contract by the consensus of the Muslims (6). And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the method of choosing an imam. Al-Nasafi begins by stating that since explicit designation (nass) is invalid for the caliphate, it is established by choice (ikhtiyar). He then reports a view from al-Ash'ari that if a single qualified person (mujtahid) sees the qualifications in someone and contracts the imama, it is valid and others cannot oppose. Al-Nasafi rejects the condition of consensus (ijma') for several reasons: (1) it would delay the imama at a time of need; (2) the Companions did not require consensus at the moment of choice; they only required a contract and then a pledge of allegiance (bay'a); (3) if consensus is not a condition, then numbers do not matter. He then provides two historical proofs: the incident at Saqifa where 'Umar proposed to give the pledge to Abu 'Ubayda, but Abu 'Ubayda deferred to Abu Bakr, and the pledge to Abu Bakr was accepted, showing that a single contract suffices. Also, Abu Bakr appointed 'Umar as his successor without consulting others, and the community accepted it. Thus, imama is valid with a single contract.

Key Terms
اختيار
إجماع
عقد
مبايعة
مجتهد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that consensus of all Muslims is necessary for the imama.
Correction: Al-Nasafi clarifies that consensus is not a condition; a single contract by a qualified person suffices, based on Companion practice and logical reasoning.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a reason given by al-Nasafi for rejecting consensus as a condition for imama?
A) It would cause delay.
B) The Companions did not require it.
C) It is impossible to achieve consensus.
D) Numbers do not matter if consensus is not required.

Key Takeaway
Al-Nasafi argues that requiring consensus for the appointment of an imam is unnecessary; a single contract by a qualified person is sufficient, as shown by Companion practice and practical necessity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever missed an opportunity to lead or do good because you waited for everyone to agree with you, even when the right course was clear? How does al-Nasafi's rejection of consensus challenge your hesitation?
?
The Companions acted swiftly with a single contract. Where in your life are you delaying a decision that requires courage because you seek a false sense of security in numbers?
?
If a single person’s contract is enough for imama, what does that say about your responsibility to step forward when you see a need? Are you ready to act even if others are silent?

Historical Evidence for Appointment by a Single Contract
Al-Nasafi provides two historical proofs for appointment by one contract.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two historical proofs from the early caliphate that support the view that the imama is valid with a single contract.

Core Idea
The incidents of Saqifa and Abu Bakr's appointment show that a single contract suffices.

Al-Nasafi supports the theoretical argument with two concrete examples from Islamic history: the election of Abu Bakr at Saqifa, where a single pledge from Umar and the acceptance of others sealed the imama, and the appointment of Umar by Abu Bakr without consultation. These examples demonstrate that a single contract is enough, and the community's subsequent acceptance confirms it.

Guided Path
1
Read the historical proofs
Read the Arabic and translation focusing on the two stories: Saqifa and Abu Bakr's appointment of Umar.
Note the role of Umar and Abu Ubayda.
2
Analyze the first proof at Saqifa
Identify how Umar's proposal to Abu Ubayda and Abu Ubayda's deferral led to the contract for Abu Bakr by a single contract.
Why does al-Nasafi consider this a proof?
3
Analyze the second proof
Abu Bakr appointed Umar without consultation, and the community accepted it. How does this support the view?
4
Connect to the overall argument
Understand how these examples are used to demonstrate that the imama is contracted by a single contract, and that the community's subsequent bay'a confirms it.
The phrase 'بإجماع المسلمين' at the end refers to the collective acceptance after the contract.

Source Text

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the imama requires a consensus contract from all leading figures at the moment of appointment.

Checkpoint
What do the two historical proofs demonstrate according to al-Nasafi?
A) The imama can only be established by a large group of people.
B) The imama is contracted by a single contract, and the community's acceptance follows.
C) The imama requires explicit designation from the previous imam.
D) The imama requires the consensus of all Muslims at the moment of appointment.

Key Takeaway
The historical examples of Abu Bakr at Saqifa and Umar's appointment demonstrate that the imama is established by a single contract, with community acceptance later.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see how quickly the early Muslims resolved the leadership issue with a single pledge at Saqifa, do you trust that Allah guides the community even in moments of apparent haste? What is your own response to moments of uncertainty—do you seek His guidance or rely on your own deliberation?
?
The community later accepted Abu Bakr and 'Umar's appointments even though they were not part of the initial contract. Are you quick to accept the decisions of your leaders based on trust, or do you withhold your support until you personally approve?
?
Abu 'Ubayda deferred to Abu Bakr despite being offered the pledge, prioritizing unity over personal ambition. When has your own humility prevented you from seeking personal gain for the sake of the community? What would it cost you to put others first today?

Abu Bakr's Caliphate and His Qualifications
Al-Nasafi lists Abu Bakr's qualifications and uses them to prove his rightful caliphate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rationale for Abu Bakr's rightful caliphate and the qualities that made him qualified.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr possessed all essential conditions for caliphate, and his leadership resolved critical disputes.

Al-Nasafi, after establishing the general necessity of imama, now applies the criteria to Abu Bakr. He lists the qualifications that Abu Bakr uniquely possessed, showing that his caliphate was not merely political but divinely sanctioned through the consensus of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Read the affirmation of caliphate
Read the passage and note the emphasis on 'خليفة محقا' and 'إمامًا حقا' as authoritative titles.
These terms imply obligation of obedience.
2
Identify the qualifications
List the qualities al-Nasafi mentions: Quraysh lineage, knowledge, piety, firmness, fortitude, military strategy, etc.
Compare with earlier conditions of imama.
3
Reflect on the central argument
Consider the argument that even resolving the disagreement is sufficient proof of his truthfulness.
This shows divine support for his caliphate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا(۱) ثبت بما تقدم من وجوب الإمامة والشرائط التي من اتصف بها صلح للإمامة نقول بعد ذلك : إن أبا بكر الله كان بعد رسول الله عليه السلام خليفة محقا وإمامًا حقا مفترض الطاعة واجب الاتباع فيما يورده ويصدره ويأمر به وينهى عنه. الصديق مستجمع لشرائط الخلافة بعد الرسول ]: وذلك لأنه له الله استجمع شرائط صحة الخلافة، فإنه كان قرشيًا لا ريبة لأحد (٢) فيه، وكان من وراء ذلك من العلم والديانة والصلابة ورباطة الجأش، والعلم بتدابير الحروب، والقيام بتهيئة الجيوش، وتنفيذ السرايا ومعرفة سياسة العامة، وتسوية أمور الرعية، كله كان ثابتا ولهذا اختارته الصحابة، وانقادوا لأوامره على ما نبين، ولو لم يكن من بركة أيامه ويُمن تعينه إلا الارتفاع ما وقع من الاختلاف بين الصحابة لكان ذلك دليلاً كافيًا على كونه محقا فيما تولى هاديًا مهديًا فيما يفعل ويأمر. ثم أول (۳) خلاف وقع بين الأمة كان الخلاف في وفاة النبي ، فإن عمر كان يقول : إنه عليه السلام لم يمت وإن من قال إنه مات أفعل به كذا وكذا، إلى أن أتى أبو بكر الصديق وأخبر أنه مات وتلا قوله تعالى: {إِنَّكَ مَيِّتٌ وَإِنَّهُم مَّيِّتُونَ ) (٤) ثم صعد للمنبر وخطب وقال في خطبته - ألا من كان يعبد محمدًا فإن محمدًا قد مات ومن كان يعبد رب محمد فإن رب محمد حي لا يموت فاجتمع الناس على موته عليه السلام. ثم اختلفوا في موضع دفنه فأشار المهاجرون إلى أن يدفن بمكة، لأنها
And when (1) it has been established by what has preceded concerning the obligation of the imama and the conditions by which whoever is qualified becomes suitable for the imama, we say after that: Indeed, Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) after the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was a true caliph and a rightful imam, obedience to whom is obligatory, and following him in what he presents, issues, commands, and forbids is necessary. As-Siddiq possessed the conditions of the caliphate after the Messenger: because he (may Allah be pleased with him) had gathered the conditions of the soundness of the caliphate. He was a Qurayshi, no one had any doubt (2) about him. Beyond that, he had knowledge, piety, firmness, fortitude, knowledge of war strategies, undertaking the preparation of armies, executing expeditions, knowledge of public policy, and managing the affairs of the subjects—all of this was established. For this reason, the Companions chose him and submitted to his commands as we will explain. If there had been no other blessing of his days and good fortune of his appointment except the raising of the disagreement that occurred among the Companions, that would be sufficient evidence that he was truthful in what he undertook, a guide and rightly guided in what he did and commanded. Then the first (3) disagreement that occurred among the community was the disagreement concerning the death of the Prophet (peace be upon him). 'Umar was saying that he (peace be upon him) had not died, and that whoever said he died would do such and such, until Abu Bakr as-Siddiq came and announced that he had died and recited the words of Allah Most High: {Indeed, you are to die, and indeed they are to die} (4). Then he ascended the pulpit and delivered a sermon, saying in his sermon: 'Behold, whoever used to worship Muhammad, indeed Muhammad has died; and whoever used to worship the Lord of Muhammad, indeed the Lord of Muhammad is Living and does not die.' So the people united on his (peace be upon him) death. Then they disagreed concerning the place of his burial; the Emigrants (Muhajirun) suggested that he be buried in Mecca, because it...
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal affirmation of Abu Bakr's caliphate. Al-Nasafi, after a brief reference to the previous discussion on the necessity of imama and its conditions, asserts that Abu Bakr was a true caliph and rightful imam whose obedience is obligatory. He then lists the conditions of the caliphate that Abu Bakr possessed: Quraysh lineage (no doubt about it), knowledge, piety, firmness, fortitude, military knowledge, ability to organize armies and expeditions, public policy, and administration of subjects. The Companions chose him for these reasons. Interestingly, al-Nasafi argues that even if there were no other blessing of his caliphate except the resolution of the disagreement that occurred among the Companions, that alone would be sufficient evidence of his truthfulness and guidance. He then narrates the first disagreement after the Prophet's death: 'Umar initially denied the Prophet's death, but Abu Bakr came, recited the Quranic verse (39:30), and gave a famous sermon declaring that the Prophet had died and that only God is immortal, which united the people. The passage ends with the beginning of the discussion on the burial place, where the Muhajirun suggested Mecca.

Key Terms
خليفة
شرائط الخلافة
الصديق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that Abu Bakr's caliphate was merely a political arrangement.
Correction: Al-Nasafi emphasizes that he possessed all essential qualifications and resolved critical disputes, proving his rightful leadership.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is not among the qualifications al-Nasafi lists for Abu Bakr?
A) He was a Qurayshi.
B) He had knowledge of public policy.
C) He was wealthy.
D) He had piety.

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's caliphate is legitimized by his possession of all required conditions and by his providential role in resolving the first major dispute after the Prophet's death.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly accept the caliphate of Abu Bakr as divinely guided, or do you harbor doubts based on modern political assumptions? What would it mean for your obedience to follow a leader whose qualifications are not worldly but spiritually validated?
?
The dispute among the Companions could have torn the Ummah apart, but Abu Bakr's leadership resolved it. Are you, in your own life, a source of unity or division for those around you? What step will you take this week to actively reconcile a relationship you have allowed to break?
?
Al-Nasafi argues that Abu Bakr's very appointment is a blessing because it resolved conflict. Do you see the hand of Allah in the leadership of your own community, or do you only see human politics? How can you cultivate a deeper trust in divine selection?

The First Dispute: The Prophet's Death and Abu Bakr's Role
Al-Nasafi narrates the first disagreement and shows Abu Bakr's pivotal role in resolving it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Abu Bakr resolved the initial disagreement about the Prophet's death, establishing his leadership.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr's firm declaration of the Prophet's death united the community and demonstrated his rightful authority.

After affirming Abu Bakr's qualifications, al-Nasafi narrates the first dispute after the Prophet's death: whether the Prophet had died. 'Umar initially denied it, but Abu Bakr recited the Quranic verse and delivered a sermon that brought consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the account of the dispute
Read the passage about the first disagreement. Notice that 'Umar initially denied the Prophet's death and threatened those who claimed it.
The dispute was serious and could have caused division.
2
Identify Abu Bakr's actions
Note that Abu Bakr came, recited the Quranic verse (39:30), and then gave a sermon that distinguished worship of the Prophet from worship of God.
His approach combined divine text and wise counsel.
3
Understand the outcome
The people united on the reality of the Prophet's death. This event is presented as evidence of Abu Bakr's guided leadership.
Al-Nasafi uses this to support his earlier argument.

وإذا(۱) ثبت بما تقدم من وجوب الإمامة والشرائط التي من اتصف بها صلح للإمامة نقول بعد ذلك : إن أبا بكر الله كان بعد رسول الله عليه السلام خليفة محقا وإمامًا حقا مفترض الطاعة واجب الاتباع فيما يورده ويصدره ويأمر به وينهى عنه. الصديق مستجمع لشرائط الخلافة بعد الرسول ]: وذلك لأنه له الله استجمع شرائط صحة الخلافة، فإنه كان قرشيًا لا ريبة لأحد (٢) فيه، وكان من وراء ذلك من العلم والديانة والصلابة ورباطة الجأش، والعلم بتدابير الحروب، والقيام بتهيئة الجيوش، وتنفيذ السرايا ومعرفة سياسة العامة، وتسوية أمور الرعية، كله كان ثابتا ولهذا اختارته الصحابة، وانقادوا لأوامره على ما نبين، ولو لم يكن من بركة أيامه ويُمن تعينه إلا الارتفاع ما وقع من الاختلاف بين الصحابة لكان ذلك دليلاً كافيًا على كونه محقا فيما تولى هاديًا مهديًا فيما يفعل ويأمر. ثم أول (۳) خلاف وقع بين الأمة كان الخلاف في وفاة النبي ، فإن عمر كان يقول : إنه عليه السلام لم يمت وإن من قال إنه مات أفعل به كذا وكذا، إلى أن أتى أبو بكر الصديق وأخبر أنه مات وتلا قوله تعالى: {إِنَّكَ مَيِّتٌ وَإِنَّهُم مَّيِّتُونَ ) (٤) ثم صعد للمنبر وخطب وقال في خطبته - ألا من كان يعبد محمدًا فإن محمدًا قد مات ومن كان يعبد رب محمد فإن رب محمد حي لا يموت فاجتمع الناس على موته عليه السلام. ثم اختلفوا في موضع دفنه فأشار المهاجرون إلى أن يدفن بمكة، لأنها
And when (1) it has been established by what has preceded concerning the obligation of the imama and the conditions by which whoever is qualified becomes suitable for the imama, we say after that: Indeed, Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) after the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was a true caliph and a rightful imam, obedience to whom is obligatory, and following him in what he presents, issues, commands, and forbids is necessary. As-Siddiq possessed the conditions of the caliphate after the Messenger: because he (may Allah be pleased with him) had gathered the conditions of the soundness of the caliphate. He was a Qurayshi, no one had any doubt (2) about him. Beyond that, he had knowledge, piety, firmness, fortitude, knowledge of war strategies, undertaking the preparation of armies, executing expeditions, knowledge of public policy, and managing the affairs of the subjects—all of this was established. For this reason, the Companions chose him and submitted to his commands as we will explain. If there had been no other blessing of his days and good fortune of his appointment except the raising of the disagreement that occurred among the Companions, that would be sufficient evidence that he was truthful in what he undertook, a guide and rightly guided in what he did and commanded. Then the first (3) disagreement that occurred among the community was the disagreement concerning the death of the Prophet (peace be upon him). 'Umar was saying that he (peace be upon him) had not died, and that whoever said he died would do such and such, until Abu Bakr as-Siddiq came and announced that he had died and recited the words of Allah Most High: {Indeed, you are to die, and indeed they are to die} (4). Then he ascended the pulpit and delivered a sermon, saying in his sermon: 'Behold, whoever used to worship Muhammad, indeed Muhammad has died; and whoever used to worship the Lord of Muhammad, indeed the Lord of Muhammad is Living and does not die.' So the people united on his (peace be upon him) death. Then they disagreed concerning the place of his burial; the Emigrants (Muhajirun) suggested that he be buried in Mecca, because it...
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal affirmation of Abu Bakr's caliphate. Al-Nasafi, after a brief reference to the previous discussion on the necessity of imama and its conditions, asserts that Abu Bakr was a true caliph and rightful imam whose obedience is obligatory. He then lists the conditions of the caliphate that Abu Bakr possessed: Quraysh lineage (no doubt about it), knowledge, piety, firmness, fortitude, military knowledge, ability to organize armies and expeditions, public policy, and administration of subjects. The Companions chose him for these reasons. Interestingly, al-Nasafi argues that even if there were no other blessing of his caliphate except the resolution of the disagreement that occurred among the Companions, that alone would be sufficient evidence of his truthfulness and guidance. He then narrates the first disagreement after the Prophet's death: 'Umar initially denied the Prophet's death, but Abu Bakr came, recited the Quranic verse (39:30), and gave a famous sermon declaring that the Prophet had died and that only God is immortal, which united the people. The passage ends with the beginning of the discussion on the burial place, where the Muhajirun suggested Mecca.

Key Terms
اختلاف
موت النبي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Abu Bakr imposed his view by force or coercion.
Correction: The passage shows he used Quranic evidence and persuasive speech, not force.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi, what was the first disagreement after the Prophet's death?
A) Whether to bury him in Mecca or Medina.
B) Whether the Prophet had died.
C) Who should be the caliph.
D) Whether to continue the expeditions.

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's decisive and divinely inspired response to the crisis of the Prophet's death established his authority and unified the community.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a crisis of certainty, do you instinctively cling to your assumptions like 'Umar did, or do you seek the truth like Abu Bakr? What is one specific way you can ensure you prioritize Quranic evidence over your emotions this week?
?
Abu Bakr's first act was to redirect the community's focus to worship of Allah alone. Is there any person, status, or desire in your life that you have unconsciously elevated to a level of worship? What concrete step will you take today to realign your heart?
?
The community united after Abu Bakr's speech. Are you a source of unity or division in your family or community? What one action can you take before this week ends to bring people together around the truth of this lesson?

The Qualifications of Abu Bakr as-Siddiq
The author states the claim of Abu Bakr's caliphate and lists his qualifications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the qualifications that made Abu Bakr the rightful caliph after the Prophet.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr possessed all conditions of caliphate, making his leadership divinely guided.

Before proving Abu Bakr's caliphate, the author first establishes that imama is obligatory and has specific conditions. He then asserts that Abu Bakr fully met these conditions, citing his lineage, knowledge, piety, military skill, and administrative ability. This lesson examines that foundational claim and the evidence of the Companions' consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get an overview. Then read the translation to understand the literal meaning.
Focus on the list of qualifications.
2
Identify the conditions
List the conditions of caliphate that the author mentions: Qurayshi lineage, knowledge, piety, firmness, military strategy, etc.
The author states that Abu Bakr possessed all of them.
3
Understand the argument
Notice the author's reasoning: because Abu Bakr had these qualities, the Companions chose him and obeyed him. Also note the additional argument that removing disagreement is sufficient proof.
This connects qualification to rightful caliphate.
4
Reflect on the claim
Consider why the author begins with this statement before providing historical examples. It establishes the principle.

الكلام في إمامة أبي بكر : وإذا ثبت بما تقدم من وجوب الإمامة والشرائط التي من اتصف بها صلح للإمامة نقول بعد ذلك : إن أبا بكر الصديق رضي الله عنه كان بعد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم خليفة محقا وإمامًا حقا مفترض الطاعة واجب الاتباع فيما يورده ويصدره ويأمر به وينهى عنه. وذلك لأنه رضي الله عنه استجمع شرائط صحة الخلافة، فإنه كان قرشيًا لا ريبة لأحد فيه، وكان من وراء ذلك من العلم والديانة والصلابة ورباطة الجأش، والعلم بتدابير الحروب، والقيام بتهيئة الجيوش، وتنفيذ السرايا ومعرفة سياسة العامة، وتسوية أمور الرعية، كله كان ثابتا ولهذا اختارته الصحابة، وانقادوا لأوامره على ما نبين، ولو لم يكن من بركة أيامه ويُمن تعينه إلا الارتفاع ما وقع من الاختلاف بين الصحابة لكان ذلك دليلاً كافيًا على كونه محقا فيما تولى هاديًا مهديًا فيما يفعل ويأمر.

فإن أول خلاف وقع بين الأمة كان الخلاف في وفاة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، فإن عمر رضي الله عنه كان يقول : إنه عليه السلام لم يمت وإن من قال إنه مات أفعل به كذا وكذا، إلى أن أتى أبو بكر الصديق وأخبر أنه مات وتلا قوله تعالى: {إِنَّكَ مَيِّتٌ وَإِنَّهُم مَّيِّتُونَ} ثم صعد المنبر وخطب وقال في خطبته: ألا من كان يعبد محمدًا فإن محمدًا قد مات ومن كان يعبد رب محمد فإن رب محمد حي لا يموت فاجتمع الناس على موته عليه السلام.

ثم اختلفوا في موضع دفنه فأشار المهاجرون إلى أن يدفن بمكة، لأنها منشؤه وبلد آبائه، وبعضهم أشاروا إلى نقله إلى مقابر الأنبياء ببيت المقدس، والأنصار قالوا إنه يدفن بالمدينة التي هي دار هجرته ومكان ظهور ملته وانتشار دعوته إلى أن روى أبو بكر الصديق رضي الله عنه: "الأنبياء يدفنون حيث يقبضون" فقبلوا روايته وارتفع الخلاف ببركته.

ثم اختلفوا في أمر الخلافة فكان الأنصار يقولون : منا أمير ومنكم أمير، وبعضهم كانوا يميلون إلى العباس، وبعضهم يرون عليا رضي الله عنه أحق بذلك، ثم ارتفع الخلاف واتفقت الآراء واجتمعت على أبي بكر رضي الله عنه، إما لما علموا بإشارة الكتاب أو الأحاديث على ما نبين وإما استدلالاً منهم بتفويض النبي عليه السلام إقامة ما هو من أعظم أركان الدين وهو الصلاة إليه، وأمره إياه بأن يحج بالناس سنة تسع عند قعوده عليه السلام عن إقامته بنفسه لعارض شغل له، وأو بأن اللطيف الخبير جل ثناؤه وتباركت أسماؤه نظر لأمة حبيبه ومتبعي صفيه ونجيبه جمع آراءهم المختلفة وأهواءهم المشتتة على من هو أكثرهم فضلاً، وأعزهم علمًا، وأوفرهم عقلاً، وأصوبهم تدبيراً وأربطهم عند الملمات جاشا ، وأشدهم على وعد الله تعالى بإظهار الدين على الأديان اتكالاً، وأيمنهم نقيبة، وأعودهم على افتاء الخلق وطبقات الرعايا نفعًا، وأظلفهم عن الفواحش نفسا ، وأصونهم عن القبائح عرضا، وأشدهم لأمور الدين تعظيمًا، وأقدمهم إسلاما ، وأجودهم كفا، وأسمحهم، يبذل ما
The discussion on the Imamate of Abu Bakr: When it has been established by what preceded of the obligation of the Imamate and the conditions by which whoever is described with them is suitable for the Imamate, we say after that: Abu Bakr as-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with him, was after the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, a rightful caliph and a true Imam, obedience to whom is obligatory, and following him is required in what he presents and issues and commands and forbids. That is because he, may Allah be pleased with him, possessed all the conditions of the validity of the caliphate, for he was a Qurayshiite about whom no one had any doubt, and besides that he had knowledge, piety, firmness, steadfastness, knowledge of military strategies, undertaking the preparation of armies, executing military expeditions, knowledge of public administration, and settling the affairs of the subjects; all of this was established, and for this the Companions chose him and submitted to his orders as we will explain. And if there were no blessing of his days and good fortune of his appointment except the removal of the disagreement that occurred among the Companions, that would be sufficient proof that he was rightful in what he undertook, a guide and rightly guided in what he does and commands. For the first disagreement that occurred among the community was the disagreement about the death of the Prophet, peace be upon him. For 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, used to say that he, peace be upon him, had not died, and that whoever said he had died he would do such and such to him, until Abu Bakr as-Siddiq came and informed them that he had died and recited the saying of Allah Almighty: {Indeed, you are to die, and indeed, they are to die} (Az-Zumar 39:30). Then he ascended the pulpit and gave a sermon, saying in his sermon: "Lo, whoever used to worship Muhammad, then Muhammad has died; and whoever used to worship the Lord of Muhammad, then the Lord of Muhammad is Alive and does not die." So the people agreed upon his death, peace be upon him. Then they disagreed about the place of his burial. The Muhajirun suggested that he be buried in Mecca because it was his birthplace and the land of his forefathers, and some of them suggested transferring him to the graves of the prophets in Jerusalem. The Ansar said that he should be buried in Medina, which was his city of emigration and the place of the emergence of his religion and the spread of his call, until Abu Bakr as-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with him, narrated: "The prophets are buried where they die." So they accepted his narration, and the disagreement was removed by his blessing. Then they disagreed about the matter of the caliphate. The Ansar said: "From us an amir and from you an amir." Some of them inclined towards al-'Abbas, and some considered 'Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, more deserving of that. Then the disagreement was removed and the opinions agreed and united upon Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him, either because they knew an indication from the Book or the hadiths as we will explain, or by their deduction from the Prophet's, peace be upon him, delegation to him of what is among the greatest pillars of the religion, namely prayer, and his order to him to lead the people in the pilgrimage in the year nine when he, peace be upon him, stayed behind from leading it himself due to an obstacle that occupied him, or because the Kind and All-Aware, Glorified is His praise and Blessed are His names, looked after the community of His beloved and the followers of His chosen intimate and united their differing opinions and scattered inclinations upon the one who was the most excellent among them, the most knowledgeable, the most complete in intellect, the most correct in administration, the firmest in heart at calamities, the most reliant on the promise of Allah Almighty to manifest the religion over all religions, the most blessed in disposition, the most beneficial in giving legal rulings to the people and the strata of subjects, the most chaste in soul from immoralities, the most protective of honor from evil deeds, the most reverent of religious matters, the earliest in Islam, the most generous in hand, the most liberal, giving what...
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument defending the caliphate of Abu Bakr as-Siddiq. It belongs to the genre of kalam discussions on imama. The author proceeds in three steps. First, he states the claim: given that imama is obligatory and has conditions, Abu Bakr was the rightful caliph after the Prophet (saws), possessing all qualifications: Qurayshi lineage, knowledge, piety, steadfastness, military and administrative competence, etc. He specifically notes that the Companions chose him and obeyed him, and that even the removal of disagreement among them is sufficient proof of his rightness. Second, he recounts the three disputes that arose after the Prophet's death and how Abu Bakr resolved each. The first dispute was about the Prophet's death itself: 'Umar initially denied it, but Abu Bakr affirmed it by reciting the Quranic verse (39:30) and delivering a sermon that united the community. The second dispute was about the burial place: Muhajirun suggested Mecca, some suggested Jerusalem, and Ansar suggested Medina; Abu Bakr resolved it by narrating a hadith that prophets are buried where they die, and the community accepted. The third dispute was about the caliphate: Ansar proposed a shared leadership, some inclined to al-Abbas, others to Ali; but the community eventually united on Abu Bakr, either by explicit scriptural indications (to be explained later) or by deduction from the Prophet's delegation of leading prayer and pilgrimage to Abu Bakr, or by divine providence that gathered them upon the most excellent. The author then lists numerous virtues of Abu Bakr to emphasize his superiority. The passage functions as both a historical narrative and a doctrinal proof for Sunni imama.

Key Terms
إمامة
خلافة
شرائط

Checkpoint
What is the first argument the author gives for Abu Bakr's caliphate?
A) He was the closest companion of the Prophet.
B) He possessed all conditions of caliphate.
C) He was chosen by the Prophet before his death.
D) He was the only one who knew the burial place.

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's caliphate was established by his possession of all necessary qualifications, confirmed by the Companions' consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you examine the qualifications of Abu Bakr listed in this lesson (knowledge, piety, firmness, steadfastness, etc.), which one are you most deficient in? What is one specific action you will take this week to strengthen that quality in your own character as a servant of Allah?
?
The author highlights that Abu Bakr's appointment removed disagreement among the Companions. Is there a relationship, family tie, or community bond in your life where your pride or stubbornness is fueling division rather than unity? Will you take the first step to reconcile today, even if it means swallowing your ego?
?
Abu Bakr is described as 'a guide and rightly guided' (هاديًا مهديًا). In your current circle of influence—whether at work, home, or among friends—are you a guide who leads others toward truth and righteousness, or are you being swayed by their opinions and your own desires? What change must you make to become a better guide for others?

Resolving Disputes: The Prophet's Death and Burial
The author narrates how Abu Bakr resolved two disputes: the Prophet's death and burial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Abu Bakr resolved the first two disputes after the Prophet's death: the denial of his death and the disagreement over his burial place.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr's knowledge and leadership united the community in two critical moments.

After establishing Abu Bakr's qualifications, the author provides historical examples of his decisive role. The first major dispute was about whether the Prophet had actually died, with Umar initially denying it. The second was about where to bury him. Both were resolved through Abu Bakr's wisdom and authority. This lesson examines these two incidents as proofs of his rightful caliphate.

Guided Path
1
Read the two disputes
Read the passage describing the dispute over the Prophet's death and the dispute over his burial. Note how each started and how Abu Bakr resolved it.
The first dispute involved Umar; the second involved different suggestions.
2
Analyze the resolution methods
For the death dispute, Abu Bakr used a Quranic verse and a sermon. For the burial, he narrated a hadith. Consider why these were effective.
Both resolutions relied on Abu Bakr's knowledge of scripture and tradition.
3
Connect to the argument
The author presents these as evidence that Abu Bakr was the rightful leader, as his actions brought unity and clarity.
This supports the claim from Lesson 1.

فإن أول خلاف وقع بين الأمة كان الخلاف في وفاة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، فإن عمر رضي الله عنه كان يقول : إنه عليه السلام لم يمت وإن من قال إنه مات أفعل به كذا وكذا، إلى أن أتى أبو بكر الصديق وأخبر أنه مات وتلا قوله تعالى: {إِنَّكَ مَيِّتٌ وَإِنَّهُم مَّيِّتُونَ} ثم صعد المنبر وخطب وقال في خطبته: ألا من كان يعبد محمدًا فإن محمدًا قد مات ومن كان يعبد رب محمد فإن رب محمد حي لا يموت فاجتمع الناس على موته عليه السلام.

ثم اختلفوا في موضع دفنه فأشار المهاجرون إلى أن يدفن بمكة، لأنها منشؤه وبلد آبائه، وبعضهم أشاروا إلى نقله إلى مقابر الأنبياء ببيت المقدس، والأنصار قالوا إنه يدفن بالمدينة التي هي دار هجرته ومكان ظهور ملته وانتشار دعوته إلى أن روى أبو بكر الصديق رضي الله عنه: "الأنبياء يدفنون حيث يقبضون" فقبلوا روايته وارتفع الخلاف ببركته.

ثم اختلفوا في أمر الخلافة فكان الأنصار يقولون : منا أمير ومنكم أمير، وبعضهم كانوا يميلون إلى العباس، وبعضهم يرون عليا رضي الله عنه أحق بذلك، ثم ارتفع الخلاف واتفقت الآراء واجتمعت على أبي بكر رضي الله عنه، إما لما علموا بإشارة الكتاب أو الأحاديث على ما نبين وإما استدلالاً منهم بتفويض النبي عليه السلام إقامة ما هو من أعظم أركان الدين وهو الصلاة إليه، وأمره إياه بأن يحج بالناس سنة تسع عند قعوده عليه السلام عن إقامته بنفسه لعارض شغل له، وأو بأن اللطيف الخبير جل ثناؤه وتباركت أسماؤه نظر لأمة حبيبه ومتبعي صفيه ونجيبه جمع آراءهم المختلفة وأهواءهم المشتتة على من هو أكثرهم فضلاً، وأعزهم علمًا، وأوفرهم عقلاً، وأصوبهم تدبيراً وأربطهم عند الملمات جاشا ، وأشدهم على وعد الله تعالى بإظهار الدين على الأديان اتكالاً، وأيمنهم نقيبة، وأعودهم على افتاء الخلق وطبقات الرعايا نفعًا، وأظلفهم عن الفواحش نفسا ، وأصونهم عن القبائح عرضا، وأشدهم لأمور الدين تعظيمًا، وأقدمهم إسلاما ، وأجودهم كفا، وأسمحهم، يبذل ما
The discussion on the Imamate of Abu Bakr: When it has been established by what preceded of the obligation of the Imamate and the conditions by which whoever is described with them is suitable for the Imamate, we say after that: Abu Bakr as-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with him, was after the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, a rightful caliph and a true Imam, obedience to whom is obligatory, and following him is required in what he presents and issues and commands and forbids. That is because he, may Allah be pleased with him, possessed all the conditions of the validity of the caliphate, for he was a Qurayshiite about whom no one had any doubt, and besides that he had knowledge, piety, firmness, steadfastness, knowledge of military strategies, undertaking the preparation of armies, executing military expeditions, knowledge of public administration, and settling the affairs of the subjects; all of this was established, and for this the Companions chose him and submitted to his orders as we will explain. And if there were no blessing of his days and good fortune of his appointment except the removal of the disagreement that occurred among the Companions, that would be sufficient proof that he was rightful in what he undertook, a guide and rightly guided in what he does and commands. For the first disagreement that occurred among the community was the disagreement about the death of the Prophet, peace be upon him. For 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, used to say that he, peace be upon him, had not died, and that whoever said he had died he would do such and such to him, until Abu Bakr as-Siddiq came and informed them that he had died and recited the saying of Allah Almighty: {Indeed, you are to die, and indeed, they are to die} (Az-Zumar 39:30). Then he ascended the pulpit and gave a sermon, saying in his sermon: "Lo, whoever used to worship Muhammad, then Muhammad has died; and whoever used to worship the Lord of Muhammad, then the Lord of Muhammad is Alive and does not die." So the people agreed upon his death, peace be upon him. Then they disagreed about the place of his burial. The Muhajirun suggested that he be buried in Mecca because it was his birthplace and the land of his forefathers, and some of them suggested transferring him to the graves of the prophets in Jerusalem. The Ansar said that he should be buried in Medina, which was his city of emigration and the place of the emergence of his religion and the spread of his call, until Abu Bakr as-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with him, narrated: "The prophets are buried where they die." So they accepted his narration, and the disagreement was removed by his blessing. Then they disagreed about the matter of the caliphate. The Ansar said: "From us an amir and from you an amir." Some of them inclined towards al-'Abbas, and some considered 'Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, more deserving of that. Then the disagreement was removed and the opinions agreed and united upon Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him, either because they knew an indication from the Book or the hadiths as we will explain, or by their deduction from the Prophet's, peace be upon him, delegation to him of what is among the greatest pillars of the religion, namely prayer, and his order to him to lead the people in the pilgrimage in the year nine when he, peace be upon him, stayed behind from leading it himself due to an obstacle that occupied him, or because the Kind and All-Aware, Glorified is His praise and Blessed are His names, looked after the community of His beloved and the followers of His chosen intimate and united their differing opinions and scattered inclinations upon the one who was the most excellent among them, the most knowledgeable, the most complete in intellect, the most correct in administration, the firmest in heart at calamities, the most reliant on the promise of Allah Almighty to manifest the religion over all religions, the most blessed in disposition, the most beneficial in giving legal rulings to the people and the strata of subjects, the most chaste in soul from immoralities, the most protective of honor from evil deeds, the most reverent of religious matters, the earliest in Islam, the most generous in hand, the most liberal, giving what...
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument defending the caliphate of Abu Bakr as-Siddiq. It belongs to the genre of kalam discussions on imama. The author proceeds in three steps. First, he states the claim: given that imama is obligatory and has conditions, Abu Bakr was the rightful caliph after the Prophet (saws), possessing all qualifications: Qurayshi lineage, knowledge, piety, steadfastness, military and administrative competence, etc. He specifically notes that the Companions chose him and obeyed him, and that even the removal of disagreement among them is sufficient proof of his rightness. Second, he recounts the three disputes that arose after the Prophet's death and how Abu Bakr resolved each. The first dispute was about the Prophet's death itself: 'Umar initially denied it, but Abu Bakr affirmed it by reciting the Quranic verse (39:30) and delivering a sermon that united the community. The second dispute was about the burial place: Muhajirun suggested Mecca, some suggested Jerusalem, and Ansar suggested Medina; Abu Bakr resolved it by narrating a hadith that prophets are buried where they die, and the community accepted. The third dispute was about the caliphate: Ansar proposed a shared leadership, some inclined to al-Abbas, others to Ali; but the community eventually united on Abu Bakr, either by explicit scriptural indications (to be explained later) or by deduction from the Prophet's delegation of leading prayer and pilgrimage to Abu Bakr, or by divine providence that gathered them upon the most excellent. The author then lists numerous virtues of Abu Bakr to emphasize his superiority. The passage functions as both a historical narrative and a doctrinal proof for Sunni imama.

Key Terms
وفاة
دفن
خلاف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Umar's denial of the Prophet's death was a sign of disbelief, but it was a moment of shock and love.
Correction: The text shows Umar was overwhelmed but later accepted Abu Bakr's evidence.

Checkpoint
How did Abu Bakr resolve the dispute about the Prophet's death?
A) He brought witnesses from the Companions.
B) He recited a Quranic verse about death and gave a sermon.
C) He appointed a committee to investigate.
D) He consulted the Ansar and Muhajirun.

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's application of Quran and hadith resolved the first two disputes, demonstrating his divinely guided leadership.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are in a disagreement within your community, do you actively seek resolution through the Quran and Sunnah, or do you cling to your own opinion? What would it take for you to put your pride aside for the sake of unity?
?
Umar's initial denial came from his deep love for the Prophet. Is there any person or thing you love so much that you struggle to accept Allah's decree regarding them? How can you train your heart to submit fully, even when it hurts?
?
Abu Bakr, through his calm knowledge, brought peace to the entire community. In your own circle—family, friends, or mosque—are you a source of healing or a source of conflict? What specific action will you take this week to be a peacemaker like Abu Bakr?

The Caliphate Dispute and the Virtues of Abu Bakr
The author narrates the resolution of the caliphate dispute and lists Abu Bakr's virtues.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the dispute over the caliphate was resolved in favor of Abu Bakr and the virtues that qualified him for leadership.

Core Idea
Through divine providence and Abu Bakr's merits, the community united upon him as caliph.

The third and most important dispute was about who should succeed the Prophet. The Ansar proposed a shared leadership, while some favored al-Abbas or Ali. Ultimately, the community agreed on Abu Bakr. The author attributes this to scriptural indications, the Prophet's delegation of prayer and pilgrimage to Abu Bakr, and divine providence guiding the people to the most excellent. This lesson also presents a list of Abu Bakr's virtues that the author began to enumerate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the passage describing the caliphate dispute and the reasons for Abu Bakr's selection. Then review the list of virtues.
The passage is incomplete; the list cuts off.
2
Identify the factors
Note the three factors mentioned: scriptural indications, delegation of prayer and pilgrimage, and divine providence. Understand how each points to Abu Bakr.
The author presents these as possible reasons.
3
Examine the virtues
The author lists many virtues of Abu Bakr: most excellent, knowledgeable, intelligent, good administrator, firm, reliant on Allah, etc. Reflect on how these qualify him.
This is a typical kalam argument: the most qualified should lead.

الكلام في إمامة أبي بكر : وإذا ثبت بما تقدم من وجوب الإمامة والشرائط التي من اتصف بها صلح للإمامة نقول بعد ذلك : إن أبا بكر الصديق رضي الله عنه كان بعد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم خليفة محقا وإمامًا حقا مفترض الطاعة واجب الاتباع فيما يورده ويصدره ويأمر به وينهى عنه. وذلك لأنه رضي الله عنه استجمع شرائط صحة الخلافة، فإنه كان قرشيًا لا ريبة لأحد فيه، وكان من وراء ذلك من العلم والديانة والصلابة ورباطة الجأش، والعلم بتدابير الحروب، والقيام بتهيئة الجيوش، وتنفيذ السرايا ومعرفة سياسة العامة، وتسوية أمور الرعية، كله كان ثابتا ولهذا اختارته الصحابة، وانقادوا لأوامره على ما نبين، ولو لم يكن من بركة أيامه ويُمن تعينه إلا الارتفاع ما وقع من الاختلاف بين الصحابة لكان ذلك دليلاً كافيًا على كونه محقا فيما تولى هاديًا مهديًا فيما يفعل ويأمر.

فإن أول خلاف وقع بين الأمة كان الخلاف في وفاة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، فإن عمر رضي الله عنه كان يقول : إنه عليه السلام لم يمت وإن من قال إنه مات أفعل به كذا وكذا، إلى أن أتى أبو بكر الصديق وأخبر أنه مات وتلا قوله تعالى: {إِنَّكَ مَيِّتٌ وَإِنَّهُم مَّيِّتُونَ} ثم صعد المنبر وخطب وقال في خطبته: ألا من كان يعبد محمدًا فإن محمدًا قد مات ومن كان يعبد رب محمد فإن رب محمد حي لا يموت فاجتمع الناس على موته عليه السلام.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that Allah guided the early community to unite on Abu Bakr? If you hold this belief, does it shape how you view the history of Islam? What would it take for you to trust that even today, Allah guides the affairs of the Muslims in ways you may not understand?
?
The passage lists many virtues of Abu Bakr: knowledge, intellect, firmness, reliance on Allah, etc. Honestly, which of these virtues do you see lacking in yourself? What is the one practical step you can take this week to cultivate that virtue, knowing that it was these qualities that made him the chosen leader?
?
If divine providence resolved the caliphate dispute, what does that imply about your own disagreements with fellow Muslims? Are you willing to submit your own opinions to the possibility that Allah's plan may be different from your preferences? What would that look like in your next conflict?

Sects and Disagreements
beginner
